style="">\xe2\x80\x94Broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Bob_Costas" title="Bob Costas">Bob Costas</a>, on Musial<sup id="cite_ref-espnclassic_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnclassic-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>At the time of his retirement, Musial held or shared 17 major league records, 29 NL records, and nine All-Star Game records.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Among those records, he ranked as the major league career leader in extra-base hits (1,377) and <a href="/wiki/Total_bases" title="Total bases">total bases</a> (6,134).<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche197_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche197-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> He also held NL career marks in categories such as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_hit_records" title="List of Major League Baseball hit records">hits (3,630)</a>, games played (3,026), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_doubles_records" title="List of Major League Baseball doubles records">doubles (725)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_runs_batted_in_records" title="List of Major League Baseball runs batted in records">RBI (1,951)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche197_145-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche197-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> He finished his career with <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_home_run_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career home run leaders">475 home runs</a> despite never having led the NL in the category.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche197_145-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche197-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>  Jerry Lansche speculates Musial would likely have become the second player, after <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>, with 2,000 RBI, and would have exceeded 500 career home runs had he not served in the military.<sup id="cite_ref-bullock2004_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullock2004-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>  His lowest full season RBI output before the war was 72 (in 1942) and as he needed only 49 RBI to reach 2,000 for his full career, he certainly would have exceeded 2,000 RBI by playing without injury in 1945.  His home run production is a different story and it is highly unlikely he would have reached 500.  He did not hit more than 13 home runs in any season before he entered the navy and did not hit as many as 25 (the number he would have needed to become a 500 career homer club member) until 1948, 3 years after returning to baseball from World War II.  His career hit total was evenly split between 1,815 hits at home and 1,815 hits on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-sabr_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sabr-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>  Steven R. Bullock speculates that it is possible that without military service Musial might have continued playing to attempt to exceed <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a>\'s career hit record of 4,191.<sup id="cite_ref-bullock2004_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullock2004-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>   Even if Musial had hit safely 207 times (the average of his hits in the 2 years before and the 2 years after his service in the navy) in 1945, he still would have been 354 hits short of tying Ty.   His hit total in his last season at age 42 was only 86; even if he could have had 103 hits a season (the average of his last 5 seasons) he would have had to play to age 47 to attain the hits record.\n</p><p>He was the first major league player to appear in more than 1,000 games at two different positions, registering 1,896 games in the outfield and 1,016 at first base.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Since Musial\'s retirement in 1963, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gwynn" title="Tony Gwynn">Tony Gwynn</a> has been the only player to finish his career with a higher <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_batting_average_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career batting average leaders">lifetime batting average</a>. Hank Aaron has been the only player to surpass his record of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_total_bases_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career total bases leaders">6,134 total bases</a>.\n</p><p>In Musial\'s 3,026 major league appearances, he was never ejected from a game.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche_1994:_14_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche_1994:_14-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Speaking about his quiet reputation within the sport\'s history, sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Bob_Costas" title="Bob Costas">Bob Costas</a> said, "He didn\'t <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">hit a homer in his last at-bat</a>; he hit a single. He didn\'t <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">hit in 56 straight games</a>. He married his high school sweetheart and stayed married to her. ... All Musial represents is more than two decades of sustained excellence and complete decency as a human being."<sup id="cite_ref-espnclassic_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnclassic-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-playing_career_and_family_life">Post-playing career and family life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-playing career and family life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Musial was named a vice president of the St. Louis Cardinals in September 1963, and he remained in that position until after the 1966 season.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche199_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche199-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> From February 1964 to January 1967, he also served as President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a>\'s physical fitness adviser, a part-time position created to promote better fitness among American citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Before the 1967 season began, the Cardinals named Musial the team\'s <a href="/wiki/General_manager_(baseball)" title="General manager (baseball)">general manager</a>, and he oversaw the club\'s <a href="/wiki/1967_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1967 St. Louis Cardinals season">World Series championship that year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche199_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche199-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> He won the allegiance of Cardinals players by making fair offers from the outset of player-contract negotiations and creating an in-stadium babysitting service so players\' wives could attend games.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> His longtime business partner Biggie Garagnani died in June 1967, prompting Musial to devote more time to managing his restaurant and other business interests.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche200_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche200-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> He came to realize that the detail-oriented desk job was not his forte. He consequently decided to step down as general manager, before even completing a full year on the job.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche200_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche200-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Musial\xe2\x80\x94like <a href="/wiki/Harmonica_Incident" title="Harmonica Incident">Phil Linz</a>\xe2\x80\x94was noted for his harmonica playing, which included his rendition of "<a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Out_to_the_Ball_Game" title="Take Me Out to the Ball Game">Take Me Out to the Ball Game</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Through the 1990s, he frequently played the harmonica at public gatherings, such as the annual Baseball Hall of Fame induction ceremony and various charity events.<sup id="cite_ref-Gig299_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gig299-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> He performed on the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Hee_Haw" title="Hee Haw">Hee Haw</a></i> and in 1994 recorded 18 songs that were sold in tandem with a harmonica-playing instruction booklet.<sup id="cite_ref-Gig299_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gig299-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Even though Musial left Donora after high school, he retained close ties to the town throughout the rest of his life. He maintained membership in local social clubs, and regularly sent a local <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">doctor</a> boxes of autographed baseballs, with the town\'s mayor using some for <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way</a> fundraising.<sup id="cite_ref-Timmermann_1-25-2013_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timmermann_1-25-2013-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Musial also gave free meals at the restaurant he owned in St. Louis to any customers who presented valid ID proving they were Donora residents.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Musial met Lillian Susan Labash, the daughter of a local grocer,<sup id="cite_ref-Timmermann_1-25-2013_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timmermann_1-25-2013-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> in Donora when both were 15, and married her in <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St._Paul_(Daytona_Beach,_Florida)" title="Basilica of St. Paul (Daytona Beach, Florida)">St. Paul\'s Catholic Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach, Florida</a> on May 25, 1940. They had four children: son Richard, and daughters Gerry, Janet, and Jeanie.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche_1994:_14_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche_1994:_14-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Lillian Musial died at 91, on May 3, 2012; their marriage had lasted for almost 72 years.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>  In his final years, Musial suffered from <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer&#39;s disease">Alzheimer\'s disease</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_and_recognition">Honors and recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Honors and recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:27%;&#32;; padding:8px"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Here stands baseball\'s perfect warrior. Here stands baseball\'s perfect knight."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Quote inscribed on the base of Musial\'s statue, attributed to former commissioner Ford Frick<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>On August 4, 1968, a statue of Musial was erected outside of <a href="/wiki/Busch_Memorial_Stadium" title="Busch Memorial Stadium">Busch Memorial Stadium</a> on the northeast grounds of the St. Louis stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche200_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche200-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The statue was moved from its original location to the west side of the new <a href="/wiki/Busch_Stadium" title="Busch Stadium">Busch Stadium</a> for its first season in 2006, where it became a popular meeting place for generations of Cardinals fans.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Musial\'s statue is inscribed with a quote attributed to former baseball commissioner <a href="/wiki/Ford_Frick" title="Ford Frick">Ford Frick</a>: "Here stands baseball\'s perfect warrior. Here stands baseball\'s perfect knight."<sup id="cite_ref-Lansche200_153-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lansche200-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Musial was elected to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> in his first year of eligibility in <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_balloting,_1969" title="Baseball Hall of Fame balloting, 1969">1969</a>, when he was named on 93.2&#160;percent of the ballots.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On June 14, 1973 he was the first inductee into the National Polish-American Hall of Fame, housed at St.&#160;Mary\'s College in Orchard Lake, Michigan. In 1989, he was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Walk_of_Fame" title="St. Louis Walk of Fame">St. Louis Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Five years later, a baseball field was named after him in his hometown of Donora.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> He was ranked tenth on <i>The Sporting News</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> list of the 100 Greatest Baseball Players published in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> He was also one of the 30 players selected to the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Century_Team" title="Major League Baseball All-Century Team">Major League Baseball All-Century Team</a>, added by a special committee after he finished 11th in fan voting among outfielders.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, he was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Famous_Missourians" title="Hall of Famous Missourians">Hall of Famous Missourians</a>, and a bronze bust depicting him is on permanent display in the rotunda of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_State_Capitol" title="Missouri State Capitol">Missouri State Capitol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>  In January, 2014, the Cardinals announced Musial among 22 former players and personnel to be inducted into the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_Hall_of_Fame_Museum" title="St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum">St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum</a> for the inaugural class of <a href="/wiki/2014_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2014 St. Louis Cardinals season">2014</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/170px-Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/255px-Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg/340px-Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="822" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Musial_and_Obama_Medal_of_Freedom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Barack Obama awards the 2010 Presidential Medal of Freedom to Stan Musial in a ceremony in the East Room of the White House February 15, 2011.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nearly two decades after Musial retired, baseball statistician <a href="/wiki/Bill_James" title="Bill James">Bill James</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sabermetrics" title="Sabermetrics">sabermetrics</a> movement began providing new ways of comparing players across baseball history.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, James ranked Musial the tenth-greatest baseball player in history, and the second-best left fielder of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Baseball-Reference.com" title="Baseball-Reference.com">Baseball-Reference.com</a>, he ranks fifth all-time among hitters on the Black Ink Test, and third all-time on the Gray Ink Test\xe2\x80\x94measures designed to compare players of different eras.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_47-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> He ranks first on Baseball-Reference\'s Hall of Fame Monitor Test, and is tied for second in the Hall of Fame Career Standards Test.<sup id="cite_ref-stats1_47-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats1-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Despite his statistical accomplishments, he is sometimes referred to as the most underrated or overlooked athlete in modern American sports history.<sup id="cite_ref-Stark07_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark07-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> For instance, in his analysis of baseball\'s under- and overrated players in 2007, sportswriter <a href="/wiki/Jayson_Stark" title="Jayson Stark">Jayson Stark</a> said, "I can\'t think of any all-time great in any sport who gets left out of more who\'s-the-greatest conversations than Stan Musial."<sup id="cite_ref-Stark07_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark07-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Musial threw out the first pitch in the fifth game of the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006 World Series</a> and delivered the <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_first_pitch" title="Ceremonial first pitch">ceremonial first pitch</a> ball to President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2009 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2009 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> A "Stan the Man" day was held in his honor by the Cardinals on May 18, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, another one of the Cardinals\' greatest sluggers, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, whose nickname was "El Hombre", said he didn\'t want to be called "The Man", even in Spanish, because "There is one man that gets that respect, and that is Stan Musial." <sup id="cite_ref-TimesObit_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimesObit-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2010, the Cardinals launched a campaign to build support for awarding Musial the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> for his lifetime of achievement and service.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The campaign realized its goal, and on February 15, 2011, Musial was awarded the Presidential Medal of Freedom by President Barack Obama<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> who called him "an icon untarnished, a beloved pillar of the community, a gentleman you\'d want your kids to emulate."<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 17, 2012, Musial made his final appearance at Busch Stadium, riding in a golf cart around the warning track before Game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2012 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a>. Musial stopped at both dugouts and greeted <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Bochy" title="Bruce Bochy">Bruce Bochy</a> and Cardinals manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Matheny" title="Mike Matheny">Mike Matheny</a>. The Cardinals would go on to win Game 4 by a score of 8-3, but lost the pennant to the eventual <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">World Series</a> champion Giants.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="MLB_statistics">MLB statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: MLB statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hitting">Hitting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hitting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:400px;">\n\n<tbody><tr align="center">\n<td>Category\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Games_played" title="Games played">G</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/At_bat" title="At bat">AB</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">H</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">2B</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Triple_(baseball)" title="Triple (baseball)">3B</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">HR</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Run_(baseball)" title="Run (baseball)">R</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" class="mw-redirect" title="Runs batted in">RBI</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">BB</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">SO</a>\n</td>\n<td><a (28th)\n</td>\n<td>1,949 (9th)\n</td>\n<td>1,951 (6th)\n</td>\n<td>1,599 (13th)\n</td>\n<td>696\n</td>\n<td>.331 (32nd)\n</td>\n<td>.417 (23rd)\n</td>\n<td>.559 (20th)\n</td>\n<td>.976 (14th)\n</td>\n<td>159 (15th)\n</td>\n<td>6,134 (2nd)\n</td>\n<td>2,562 (3rd)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fielding">Fielding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span align="center">\n<td>Category\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Games_played" title="Games played">G</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Putout" title="Putout">PO</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Assist_(baseball)" class="mw-headline" id="Value">Value</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Value">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:400px;">\n\n<tbody><tr align="center">\n<td>Category\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wins_Above_Replacement#Calculation" title="Wins Above Replacement">rWAR</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wins_Above_Replacement#Calculation" title="Wins Above Replacement">fWAR</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr align="center">\n<td>Total<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><br />\n<p>(Rank among<br />\nposition players)\n</p>\n</td>\n<td>128.1<br />\n<p>(8th)\n</p>\n</td>\n<td>126.8<br />\n<p>(10th)\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On January 19, 2013, Musial died at age 92 of <a href="/wiki/Natural_causes" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural causes">natural causes</a> at his home in <a href="/wiki/Ladue,_Missouri" title="Ladue, Missouri">Ladue, Missouri</a>, on the same day as fellow MLB Hall of Fame inductee <a href="/wiki/Earl_Weaver" title="Earl Weaver">Earl Weaver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hummel_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hummel-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Musial was surrounded by his family as he died peacefully.<sup id="cite_ref-Hummel_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hummel-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Cardinals owner <a href="/wiki/William_DeWitt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William DeWitt, Jr.">Bill DeWitt, Jr.</a> released the following statement:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We have lost the most beloved member of the Cardinals family. Stan Musial was the greatest player in Cardinals history and one of the best players in the history of baseball. The entire Cardinals organization extends its sincere condolences to Stan\'s family, including his children Richard, Gerry, Janet and Jean, as well as his eleven grandchildren and twelve great grandchildren. We join fans everywhere in mourning the loss of our dear friend and reflect on how fortunate we all are to have known \'Stan the Man\'.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Upon hearing the news of his death, fans gathered and began an impromptu memorial at his statue outside Busch Stadium; the Cardinals issued a release saying the memorial would be left in place for some time.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>  In a laudatory obituary, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> quoted famed New York manager <a href="/wiki/Leo_Durocher" title="Leo Durocher">Leo Durocher</a>: "There is only one way to pitch to Musial\xe2\x80\x94under the plate."<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/Jay_Nixon" title="Jay Nixon">Jay Nixon</a> commented: "Stan Musial was a great American hero who\xe2\x80\x94with the utmost humility\xe2\x80\x94inspired us all to aim high and dream big. The world is emptier today without him, but far better to have known him. The legacy of \'baseball\'s perfect warrior\' will endure and inspire generations to come."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> Mayor <a href="/wiki/Francis_G._Slay" class="mw-redirect" title="Francis G. Slay">Francis Slay</a> tweeted: "Sad as we are, we are fortunate to have had Stan in STL for so long, and are also glad that Stan and Lil are together again." He ordered flags at half-staff in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>"Major League Baseball has lost one of its true legends in Stan Musial, a Hall of Famer in every sense and a man who led a great American life", Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> said. "He was the heart and soul of the historic St. Louis Cardinals franchise for generations, and he served his country during World War II. A recipient of the Presidential Medal of Freedom in 2011, Stan\'s life embodies baseball\'s unparalleled history and why this game is the national pastime."<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thousands of fans braved cold temperatures on January 24 for a public visitation at the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Basilica_of_Saint_Louis" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral Basilica of Saint Louis">Cathedral Basilica of Saint Louis</a>, where Musial lay in state, dressed in his trademark cardinal-red blazer and with a harmonica in his lapel pocket, flanked by a Navy honor guard. A private funeral Mass was held on Saturday, January 26, 2013, at the New Cathedral in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a>, televised locally by <a href="/wiki/KTVI" title="KTVI">KTVI</a> and <a href="/wiki/KPLR-TV" title="KPLR-TV">KPLR</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Midwest" title="Fox Sports Midwest">Fox Sports Midwest</a> on pay-television. New York\'s Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Dolan" class="mw-redirect" title="Timothy Dolan">Timothy Dolan</a>, who in his first episcopal post served as an auxiliary bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Saint_Louis" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Saint Louis">Archdiocese of Saint Louis</a>, was the principal celebrant, and Knoxville\'s Bishop <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stika" title="Richard Stika">Richard F. Stika</a>, Musial\'s former parish priest, was the <a href="/wiki/Homilist" class="mw-redirect" title="Homilist">homilist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Costas" title="Bob Costas">Bob Costas</a> gave the principal eulogy, calling him "the genuine hero who as the years and decades passed, and disillusionment came from other directions, never once let us down", and quoting fellow Cooperstown honoree <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Mantle" title="Mickey Mantle">Mickey Mantle</a>, who once said that Musial "was a better player than me because he was a better man than me".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stan_Musial&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As a reflection of his popularity, Musial has had infrastructure named after him.\nIn May 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_Senate" title="Pennsylvania State Senate">Pennsylvania State Senate</a> changed the name of the bridge that carries the C. Vance Deicas Memorial Highway (S.R. 1077) over the Monongahela River from Donora-Monessen Bridge to <a href="/wiki/Donora-Monessen_Bridge" title="Donora-Monessen Bridge">Stan Musial Bridge</a> after Musial who was a native of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Solobay2011-05-24_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solobay2011-05-24-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\nIn October 2013 the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Fire_Department" title="St. Louis Fire Department">St. Louis Fire Department</a> started operating a <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial_(fireboat)" title="Stan Musial (fireboat)">fireboat</a> named after Musial.<sup id="cite_ref-Cbs2012-05-24_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cbs2012-05-24-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\nIn July 2013, the new <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">Interstate 70</a> bridge over the Mississippi River between <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> at St. Louis received the official name of "<a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial_Veterans_Memorial_Bridge" title="Stan Musial Veterans Memorial Bridge">Stan Musial Veterans Memorial Bridge</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-law_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-law-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stan Musial is freqently referenced in John Grisham\'s novel "A Painted House", whose plot takes place on an Arkansas farm in 1952. The protagonist, a 7-year old farm boy, is an avid Cardinals fan and specifically an admirer of "Stan the Man". He follows the team\'s games on the radio every evening, and dreams of emulating Stan Musial and having a career in the Cardinals.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See
